	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Patrick Stewart</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"><div id="mw-fr-revisiontag" class="flaggedrevs_short flaggedrevs_stable_synced plainlinks noprint"><div class="flaggedrevs_short_basic"><span aria-disabled='false' title='Changes must be reviewed before being displayed on this page.' class='flaggedrevs-icon oo-ui-widget oo-ui-widget-enabled oo-ui-iconElement-icon oo-ui-icon-articleSearch oo-ui-iconElement oo-ui-labelElement-invisible oo-ui-iconWidget'></span><span id='mw-fr-revisiontoggle' aria-disabled='false' title='show/hide details' class='fr-toggle-arrow oo-ui-widget oo-ui-widget-enabled oo-ui-indicatorElement-indicator oo-ui-indicator-down oo-ui-indicatorElement oo-ui-labelElement-invisible oo-ui-indicatorWidget'></span></div>
<div id="mw-fr-revisiondetails-wrapper" style="position:relative;"><div id="mw-fr-revisiondetails" class="flaggedrevs_short_details" style="display:none">This is the <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Pending_changes" title="Wikipedia:Pending changes">latest accepted revision</a>, <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Special:Log&amp;type=review&amp;page=Patrick_Stewart">reviewed</a> on <i>25 September 2019</i>.</div>

		<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">For other people named Patrick Stewart, see <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Stewart_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Patrick Stewart (disambiguation)">Patrick Stewart (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>
<div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">English film, television and stage actor</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">

</p>

<p><b>Sir Patrick Stewart</b> <span class="noexcerpt" style="font-size:85%;"><a href="/wiki/Officer_of_the_Order_of_the_British_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Officer of the Order of the British Empire">OBE</a></span> (born 13 July 1940)<sup id="cite_ref-NPG_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NPG-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> is an English actor whose work has included roles on stage, television, and film in a career spanning almost six decades. He has been nominated for <a href="/wiki/Laurence_Olivier_Award" title="Laurence Olivier Award">Olivier</a>, <a href="/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Golden Globe Award">Golden Globe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Emmy_Award" title="Emmy Award">Emmy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Screen_Actors_Guild_Award" title="Screen Actors Guild Award">Screen Actors Guild</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Saturn_Award" title="Saturn Award">Saturn</a> Awards.
</p><p>Beginning his career with a long run with the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Shakespeare_Company" title="Royal Shakespeare Company">Royal Shakespeare Company</a>, Stewart received the 1979 <a href="/wiki/Laurence_Olivier_Award_for_Best_Actor_in_a_Supporting_Role" title="Laurence Olivier Award for Best Actor in a Supporting Role">Laurence Olivier Award for Best Actor in a Supporting Role</a> for his performance in <i><a href="/wiki/Antony_and_Cleopatra" title="Antony and Cleopatra">Antony and Cleopatra</a></i> in the <a href="/wiki/West_End_theatre" title="West End theatre">West End</a>. Stewart's first major screen roles were in <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a>-broadcast television productions during the mid-late 1970s, including <i><a href="/wiki/Hedda_(film)" title="Hedda (film)">Hedda</a></i>, and the <i><a href="/wiki/I,_Claudius_(TV_series)" title="I, Claudius (TV series)">I, Claudius</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Miniseries" title="Miniseries">miniseries</a>.
</p><p>From the 1980s onward, Stewart began working in American television and film, with prominent leading roles such as Captain <a href="/wiki/Jean-Luc_Picard" title="Jean-Luc Picard">Jean-Luc Picard</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Trek:_The_Next_Generation" title="Star Trek: The Next Generation">Star Trek: The Next Generation</a></i> and its <a href="/wiki/Star_Trek_(film_series)#The_Next_Generation_films" class="mw-redirect" title="Star Trek (film series)">subsequent films</a>, as <a href="/wiki/Professor_X" title="Professor X">Professor Charles Xavier</a> in the <a href="/wiki/X-Men_(film_series)" title="X-Men (film series)"><i>X-Men</i> series</a> of superhero films, the lead of the <a href="/wiki/Starz" title="Starz">Starz</a> TV series <i><a href="/wiki/Blunt_Talk" title="Blunt Talk">Blunt Talk</a></i>, and voice roles such as CIA Deputy Director <a href="/wiki/Avery_Bullock" class="mw-redirect" title="Avery Bullock">Avery Bullock</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/American_Dad!" title="American Dad!">American Dad!</a></i> and the narrator in <i><a href="/wiki/Ted_(film)" title="Ted (film)">Ted</a></i>. Having remained with the Royal Shakespeare Company, in 2008 Stewart played <a href="/wiki/King_Claudius" title="King Claudius">King Claudius</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/Hamlet" title="Hamlet">Hamlet</a></i> in the West End and won a second Olivier Award.
</p><p>In 1993, <i><a href="/wiki/TV_Guide" title="TV Guide">TV Guide</a></i> named Stewart the Best Dramatic Television Actor of the 1980s.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> He received a star on the <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Walk_of_Fame" title="Hollywood Walk of Fame">Hollywood Walk of Fame</a> on 16 December 1996. In 2010, Stewart was <a href="/wiki/Knight_Bachelor" title="Knight Bachelor">knighted</a> by <a href="/wiki/Queen_Elizabeth_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Queen Elizabeth II">Queen Elizabeth II</a> for services to drama.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Patrick_Stewart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bristol_Old_Vic_Scenic_Workshop_(geograph_4326778).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Bristol_Old_Vic_Scenic_Workshop_%28geograph_4326778%29.jpg/220px-Bristol_Old_Vic_Scenic_Workshop_%28geograph_4326778%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="183" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Bristol_Old_Vic_Scenic_Workshop_%28geograph_4326778%29.jpg/330px-Bristol_Old_Vic_Scenic_Workshop_%28geograph_4326778%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Bristol_Old_Vic_Scenic_Workshop_%28geograph_4326778%29.jpg/440px-Bristol_Old_Vic_Scenic_Workshop_%28geograph_4326778%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="666" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bristol_Old_Vic_Scenic_Workshop_(geograph_4326778).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Stewart attended <a href="/wiki/Bristol_Old_Vic_Theatre_School" title="Bristol Old Vic Theatre School">Bristol Old Vic Theatre School</a> in his youth.</div></div></div><p>Patrick Stewart was born on 13 July 1940<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-patrickstewart1_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-patrickstewart1-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> in <a href="/wiki/Mirfield" title="Mirfield">Mirfield</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> in the <a href="/wiki/West_Riding_of_Yorkshire" title="West Riding of Yorkshire">West Riding of Yorkshire</a>, England, to Gladys (née Barrowclough), a weaver and textile worker, and Alfred Stewart, a <a href="/wiki/Regimental_sergeant_major" title="Regimental sergeant major">regimental sergeant major</a> in the <a href="/wiki/British_Army" title="British Army">British Army</a>. He has two older brothers, Geoffrey (b. 28 January 1925, Mirfield) and Trevor (b. 10 August 1935, Mirfield).<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> His parents did not give him a middle name, but he used the middle name "Hewes" professionally for a while in the 1980s.<sup id="cite_ref-var12_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-var12-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Stewart grew up in a poor household with <a href="/wiki/Domestic_violence" title="Domestic violence">domestic violence</a> from his father, an experience which later influenced his political and ideological beliefs.<sup id="cite_ref-back_on_stage_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-back_on_stage-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> He spent much of his childhood in <a href="/wiki/Jarrow" title="Jarrow">Jarrow</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>  Stewart's father served with the <a href="/wiki/King%27s_Own_Yorkshire_Light_Infantry" title="King&#39;s Own Yorkshire Light Infantry">King's Own Yorkshire Light Infantry</a> and was regimental sergeant major of the <a href="/wiki/2nd_Battalion,_Parachute_Regiment" title="2nd Battalion, Parachute Regiment">2nd Battalion</a>, <a href="/wiki/Parachute_Regiment_(United_Kingdom)" title="Parachute Regiment (United Kingdom)">Parachute Regiment</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Second_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second World War">Second World War</a>, having previously worked as a general labourer and as a postman.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> As a result of his wartime experience during the <a href="/wiki/Dunkirk_evacuation" title="Dunkirk evacuation">Dunkirk evacuation</a>, his father suffered from what was then known as <a href="/wiki/Combat_fatigue" class="mw-redirect" title="Combat fatigue">combat fatigue</a> (related to what is now known as <a href="/wiki/Post-traumatic_stress_disorder" class="mw-redirect" title="Post-traumatic stress disorder">post-traumatic stress disorder</a>). In a 2008 interview, Stewart said, "My father was a very potent individual, a very powerful man, who got what he wanted. It was said that when he strode onto the parade ground, birds stopped singing. It was many, many years before I realised how my father inserted himself into my work. I've grown a moustache for <i><a href="/wiki/Macbeth" title="Macbeth">Macbeth</a></i>. My father didn't have one, but when I looked in the mirror just before I went on stage I saw my father's face staring straight back at me."<sup id="cite_ref-Twenty_Questions_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Twenty_Questions-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Stewart attended <a href="/wiki/Crowlees_Junior_and_Infant_School" title="Crowlees Junior and Infant School">Crowlees Church of England Junior and Infants School</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> He attributes his acting career to his English teacher, Cecil Dormand, who "put a copy of Shakespeare in my hand [and] said, 'Now get up on your feet and perform."<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_News_–_Star_Trek_star_Patrick_Stewart_knighted_at_Palace_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_News_–_Star_Trek_star_Patrick_Stewart_knighted_at_Palace-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> In 1951, aged 11, he entered Mirfield <a href="/wiki/Secondary_Modern_School" class="mw-redirect" title="Secondary Modern School">Secondary Modern School</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-mirmem_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mirmem-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> where he continued to study drama. Around the same time he met the actor <a href="/wiki/Brian_Blessed" title="Brian Blessed">Brian Blessed</a> at a <a href="/wiki/Mytholmroyd" title="Mytholmroyd">Mytholmroyd</a> drama course, and the two have been friends ever since.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>At the age of 15, Stewart left school and increased his participation in local theatre. He gained a job as a newspaper reporter and obituary writer at the <i>Mirfield &amp; District Reporter</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-stfc_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stfc-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> but after a year his employer gave him an ultimatum to choose acting or journalism,<sup id="cite_ref-thepsn_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thepsn-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> and he left the job. His brother tells the story that Stewart had been attending rehearsals during work time and then inventing the stories he reported. Stewart also trained as a boxer.<sup id="cite_ref-stfc_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stfc-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> Stewart reported that acting served as a means of self-expression in his youth.<sup id="cite_ref-ind20030630_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ind20030630-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Both Stewart and his friend Blessed later received grants to attend the <a href="/wiki/Bristol_Old_Vic_Theatre_School" title="Bristol Old Vic Theatre School">Bristol Old Vic Theatre School</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career">Career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Patrick_Stewart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span id="Early_acting_career_.281966.E2.80.931987.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_acting_career_(1966–1987)">Early acting career (1966–1987)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Patrick_Stewart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Early acting career (1966–1987)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Following a period with <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Central_Library" title="Manchester Central Library">Manchester's Library Theatre</a>, he became a member of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Shakespeare_Company" title="Royal Shakespeare Company">Royal Shakespeare Company</a> in 1966, remaining with them until 1982. He was an associate artist of the company in 1968.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> He appeared with actors such as <a href="/wiki/Ben_Kingsley" title="Ben Kingsley">Ben Kingsley</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ian_Richardson" title="Ian Richardson">Ian Richardson</a>. In January 1967, he made his debut TV appearance on <i><a href="/wiki/Coronation_Street" title="Coronation Street">Coronation Street</a></i> as a fire officer. In 1969, he had a brief TV cameo role as <a href="/wiki/Horatio_(Hamlet)" title="Horatio (Hamlet)">Horatio</a>, opposite Ian Richardson's <a href="/wiki/Hamlet" title="Hamlet">Hamlet</a>, in a performance of the gravedigger scene as part of episode six of Sir <a href="/wiki/Kenneth_Clark" title="Kenneth Clark">Kenneth Clark</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Civilisation_(TV_series)" title="Civilisation (TV series)">Civilisation</a></i> television series.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> He made his Broadway debut as <a href="/wiki/Tom_Snout" title="Tom Snout">Snout</a> in <a href="/wiki/Peter_Brook" title="Peter Brook">Peter Brook</a>'s legendary<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> production of <i><a href="/wiki/A_Midsummer_Night%27s_Dream" title="A Midsummer Night&#39;s Dream">A Midsummer Night's Dream</a>,</i> then moved to the <a href="/wiki/Royal_National_Theatre" title="Royal National Theatre">Royal National Theatre</a> in the early 1980s.
</p><p>Over the years, Stewart took roles in many major television series without ever becoming a household name. He appeared as <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin" title="Vladimir Lenin">Vladimir Lenin</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/Fall_of_Eagles" title="Fall of Eagles">Fall of Eagles</a></i>; <a href="/wiki/Sejanus" title="Sejanus">Sejanus</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/I,_Claudius_(TV_series)" title="I, Claudius (TV series)">I, Claudius</a></i>;<sup id="cite_ref-TNGComp18_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TNGComp18-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Karla_(character)" title="Karla (character)">Karla</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/Tinker_Tailor_Soldier_Spy_(miniseries)" title="Tinker Tailor Soldier Spy (miniseries)">Tinker Tailor Soldier Spy</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Smiley%27s_People_(miniseries)" title="Smiley&#39;s People (miniseries)">Smiley's People</a></i>; <a href="/wiki/King_Claudius" title="King Claudius">Claudius</a> in a 1980 BBC adaptation of <i><a href="/wiki/Hamlet" title="Hamlet">Hamlet</a></i>. He even took the romantic male lead in the 1975 <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> adaptation of <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Gaskell" title="Elizabeth Gaskell">Elizabeth Gaskell</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/North_and_South_(1854_novel)" class="mw-redirect" title="North and South (1854 novel)">North and South</a></i>. He also took the lead, playing psychiatric consultant Dr Edward Roebuck in BBC's <i>Maybury</i> in 1981. Stewart continued to play minor roles in films, such as <a href="/wiki/Leondegrance" class="mw-redirect" title="Leondegrance">King Leondegrance</a> in <a href="/wiki/John_Boorman" title="John Boorman">John Boorman</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Excalibur_(film)" title="Excalibur (film)">Excalibur</a></i> (1981),<sup id="cite_ref-TNGComp18_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TNGComp18-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> the character <a href="/wiki/Gurney_Halleck" title="Gurney Halleck">Gurney Halleck</a> in <a href="/wiki/David_Lynch" title="David Lynch">David Lynch</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Dune_(1984_film)" title="Dune (1984 film)">Dune</a></i> (1984)<sup id="cite_ref-TNGComp18_26-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TNGComp18-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> and Dr. Armstrong in <a href="/wiki/Tobe_Hooper" title="Tobe Hooper">Tobe Hooper</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Lifeforce_(film)" title="Lifeforce (film)">Lifeforce</a></i> (1985).
</p><p>Stewart preferred classical theatre to other genres, asking <i><a href="/wiki/Doctor_Who" title="Doctor Who">Doctor Who</a></i> actress <a href="/wiki/Lalla_Ward" title="Lalla Ward">Lalla Ward</a> why she would work in science fiction or on television.<sup id="cite_ref-bbcward_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbcward-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> In 1987, he nonetheless agreed to work in Hollywood on a revival of an old science-fiction television show, after <a href="/wiki/Robert_H._Justman" title="Robert H. Justman">Robert H. Justman</a> saw him while attending a literary reading at <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_Los_Angeles" title="University of California, Los Angeles">UCLA</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-brady19920405_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brady19920405-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bbcjustman_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbcjustman-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Stewart knew nothing about the original show, <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Trek:_The_Original_Series" title="Star Trek: The Original Series">Star Trek</a></i>, or its iconic status in <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_the_United_States" title="Culture of the United States">American culture</a>. He was reluctant to sign the standard contract of six years but did so as he, his agent, and others with whom Stewart consulted, all believed that the new show would quickly fail, and he would return to his London stage career after making some money.<sup id="cite_ref-lyall20080127_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lyall20080127-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-appleyard20071104_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-appleyard20071104-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bbcstewart_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbcstewart-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-day20121226_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-day20121226-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>  While in Hollywood, he briefly took a middle name, "Hewes", to differentiate himself from another Patrick Stewart who was already a member of the Screen Actors Guild.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Film_and_TV_career">Film and TV career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Patrick_Stewart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Film and TV career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Star_Trek:_The_Next_Generation"><i>Star Trek: The Next Generation</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Patrick_Stewart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Star Trek: The Next Generation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>When Stewart was picked for the role of Captain <a href="/wiki/Jean-Luc_Picard" title="Jean-Luc Picard">Jean-Luc Picard</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Trek:_The_Next_Generation" title="Star Trek: The Next Generation">Star Trek: The Next Generation</a></i> (1987–94), the <i><a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Times" title="Los Angeles Times">Los Angeles Times</a></i> called him an "unknown British Shakespearean actor". Still living out of his suitcase because of his scepticism that the show would succeed,<sup id="cite_ref-day20121226_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-day20121226-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> Stewart was unprepared for the long schedule of television production<sup id="cite_ref-bbcstewart_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbcstewart-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> that began at 4:45 am each day.<sup id="cite_ref-brady19920405_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brady19920405-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> He initially experienced difficulty fitting in with his less-disciplined castmates,<sup id="cite_ref-lyall20080127_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lyall20080127-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> saying that his "spirits used to sink" when required to memorise and recite <a href="/wiki/Technobabble" title="Technobabble">technobabble</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bbcstewart_32-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbcstewart-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Stewart eventually came to better understand the cultural differences between the stage and television,<sup id="cite_ref-lyall20080127_30-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lyall20080127-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> and his favourite technical line became "<a href="/wiki/Space-time_continuum" class="mw-redirect" title="Space-time continuum">space-time continuum</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-bbcstewart_32-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbcstewart-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> He remained close friends with his fellow <i>Star Trek</i> actors<sup id="cite_ref-lyall20080127_30-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lyall20080127-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> and became their advocate with the producers when necessary.<sup id="cite_ref-day20121226_33-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-day20121226-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Marina_Sirtis" title="Marina Sirtis">Marina Sirtis</a> credited Stewart with "at least 50%, if not more" of the show's success because others imitated his professionalism and dedication to acting.<sup id="cite_ref-sirtis_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sirtis-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="quotebox pullquote floatleft" style="width:300px;&#32;;"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r887775652">.mw-parser-output .quotebox{background-color:#F9F9F9;border:1px solid #aaa;box-sizing:border-box;padding:10px;font-size:88%;max-width:100%}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft{margin:0.5em 1.4em 0.8em 0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright{margin:0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.centered{margin:0.5em auto 0.8em auto}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft p,.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright p{font-style:inherit}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-title{background-color:#F9F9F9;text-align:center;font-size:larger;font-weight:bold}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:before{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" “ ";vertical-align:-45%;line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:after{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" ” ";line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .left-aligned{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .right-aligned{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .center-aligned{text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .quotebox cite{display:block;font-style:normal}@media screen and (max-width:360px){.mw-parser-output .quotebox{min-width:100%;margin:0 0 0.8em!important;float:none!important}}</style>
<div class="quotebox-quote left-aligned" style="">It really wasn't until the first season ended [when] I went to my first Star Trek convention ... [I] had expected that I would be standing in front of a few hundred people and found that there were two and a half thousand people and that they already knew more about me than I could ever possibly have believed.</div>
<p><cite class="right-aligned" style="">Stewart, on when he realised he had become famous<sup id="cite_ref-bbcstewart_32-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbcstewart-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup></cite>
</p>
</div>
<p>Stewart unexpectedly became wealthy because of the show's success.<sup id="cite_ref-appleyard20071104_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-appleyard20071104-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> In 1992, during a break in filming, Stewart calculated that he earned more during that break than from 10 weeks of <i>Woolf</i> in London.<sup id="cite_ref-brady19920405_28-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brady19920405-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> From 1994 to 2002, he also portrayed Picard in the films <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Trek_Generations" title="Star Trek Generations">Star Trek Generations</a></i> (1994), <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Trek:_First_Contact" title="Star Trek: First Contact">Star Trek: First Contact</a></i> (1996), <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Trek:_Insurrection" title="Star Trek: Insurrection">Star Trek: Insurrection</a></i> (1998) and <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Trek:_Nemesis" title="Star Trek: Nemesis">Star Trek: Nemesis</a></i> (2002); and in <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Trek:_Deep_Space_Nine" title="Star Trek: Deep Space Nine">Star Trek: Deep Space Nine</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s pilot episode "<a href="/wiki/Emissary_(Star_Trek:_Deep_Space_Nine)" title="Emissary (Star Trek: Deep Space Nine)">Emissary</a>", and received a 1995 <a href="/wiki/Screen_Actors_Guild" title="Screen Actors Guild">Screen Actors Guild</a> Award nomination for "Outstanding Performance by a Male Actor in a Drama Series".
</p><p>When asked in 2011 for the highlight of his career, he chose <i>Star Trek: The Next Generation</i>, because "it changed everything [for me]."<sup id="cite_ref-bbcfiveminutes_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbcfiveminutes-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> He has also said he is very proud of his work on <i>Star Trek: The Next Generation</i>, for its social message and educational impact on young viewers. When questioned about the significance of his role compared to his distinguished Shakespearean career, Stewart has said that: "The fact is all of those years in Royal Shakespeare Company – playing all those kings, emperors, princes and tragic heroes – were nothing but preparation for sitting in the captain's chair of the Enterprise."<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
The accolades Stewart has received include the readers of <i>TV Guide</i> in 1992 choosing him with <a href="/wiki/Cindy_Crawford" title="Cindy Crawford">Cindy Crawford</a>, of whom he had never heard, as television's "most bodacious" man and woman.<sup id="cite_ref-dn19920713_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dn19920713-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bbcfrakes_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbcfrakes-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ind20030630_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ind20030630-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> In an interview with <a href="/wiki/Michael_Parkinson" title="Michael Parkinson">Michael Parkinson</a>, he expressed gratitude for <a href="/wiki/Gene_Roddenberry" title="Gene Roddenberry">Gene Roddenberry</a>'s response to a reporter who said, "Surely they would have cured baldness by the 24th century," to which Roddenberry replied, "In the 24th century, they wouldn't care."<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="quotebox pullquote floatright" style="; width:40%"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r887775652"/>
<div class="quotebox-quote left-aligned" style="">"It came to a point where I had no idea where Picard began and I ended. We completely overlapped. His voice became my voice, and there were other elements of him that became me" ... No director in Hollywood wanted to cast this grand, deep-voiced, bald English guy because everybody knew he was Picard and couldn't possibly be anybody else. In the event, he effectively reprised the part as Professor Charles Xavier – a grand, deep-voiced, bald English guy – in the <i>X-Men</i> films.</div>
<p><cite class="right-aligned" style="">– Interview, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Times" title="The Times">The Times</a></i>&#160;<sup id="cite_ref-appleyard20071104_31-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-appleyard20071104-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup></cite>
</p>
</div>
<p>On 4 August 2018, CBS and Stewart jointly announced that he would be reprising his role as Jean-Luc Picard in a new <i>Star Trek</i> series. In a prepared statement, Stewart said he and the new show's producers would "endeavour to bring a fresh, unexpected and pertinent story to life once more."<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="X-Men_film_series"><i>X-Men</i> film series</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Patrick_Stewart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: X-Men film series">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The success of the <i>Star Trek: The Next Generation</i> TV and film franchises <a href="/wiki/Typecasting_(acting)" title="Typecasting (acting)">typecast</a> Stewart as Picard and obtaining other roles became difficult.<sup id="cite_ref-appleyard20071104_31-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-appleyard20071104-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-portsmouth20100413_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-portsmouth20100413-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> He also found returning to the stage difficult because of his long departure.<sup id="cite_ref-appleyard20071104_31-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-appleyard20071104-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> He commented that he would never have joined <i>The Next Generation</i> had he known that it would air for seven years: "No, no. NO. And looking back now it still frightens me a little bit to think that so much of my life was totally devoted to Star Trek and almost nothing else."<sup id="cite_ref-bbcstewart_32-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbcstewart-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>However, in the late 1990s he accepted a key role in the big-budget <a href="/wiki/X-Men_(film_series)" title="X-Men (film series)"><i>X-Men</i> film series</a>, as <a href="/wiki/Professor_X" title="Professor X">Professor Charles Xavier</a>, founder and mentor of the superhero team, a role similar in many ways to Picard.<sup id="cite_ref-appleyard20071104_31-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-appleyard20071104-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> He was initially reluctant to sign on to another movie franchise, but his interest in working with director <a href="/wiki/Bryan_Singer" title="Bryan Singer">Bryan Singer</a> persuaded him.<sup id="cite_ref-appleyard20071104_31-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-appleyard20071104-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> Stewart has played the role in seven feature films (<i><a href="/wiki/X-Men_(film)" title="X-Men (film)">X-Men</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/X2_(film)" title="X2 (film)">X2</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/X-Men:_The_Last_Stand" title="X-Men: The Last Stand">X-Men: The Last Stand</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/X-Men_Origins:_Wolverine" title="X-Men Origins: Wolverine">X-Men Origins: Wolverine</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wolverine_(film)" title="The Wolverine (film)">The Wolverine</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/X-Men:_Days_of_Future_Past" title="X-Men: Days of Future Past">X-Men: Days of Future Past</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Logan_(film)" title="Logan (film)">Logan</a></i>) and voiced the role in several video games (<i><a href="/wiki/X-Men_Legends" title="X-Men Legends">X-Men Legends</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/X-Men_Legends_II" class="mw-redirect" title="X-Men Legends II">X-Men Legends II</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/X-Men:_Next_Dimension" title="X-Men: Next Dimension">X-Men: Next Dimension</a></i>). Stewart announced that he was leaving the <i>X-Men</i> film franchise after <i><a href="/wiki/Logan_(film)" title="Logan (film)">Logan</a></i>, which was the final time he played the role.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Documentaries">Documentaries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Patrick_Stewart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Documentaries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In 2011, Stewart appeared in the feature-length documentary <i><a href="/wiki/The_Captains_(film)" title="The Captains (film)">The Captains</a></i> alongside <a href="/wiki/William_Shatner" title="William Shatner">William Shatner</a> (who played <i>Star Trek</i> Captain <a href="/wiki/James_T._Kirk" title="James T. Kirk">James Kirk</a>) – Shatner also wrote and directed the film. In the film, Shatner interviews actors who have portrayed captains within the <i>Star Trek</i> franchise. The film pays a great deal of attention to Shatner's interviews with Stewart at his home in <a href="/wiki/Oxfordshire" title="Oxfordshire">Oxfordshire</a>, as well as at a <a href="/wiki/Star_Trek_convention" class="mw-redirect" title="Star Trek convention"><i>Star Trek</i> Convention</a> in <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Valley" title="Las Vegas Valley">Las Vegas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nevada" title="Nevada">Nevada</a>; Stewart reveals the fear and personal failings that came along with his tenure as a <a href="/wiki/Starfleet" title="Starfleet">Starfleet</a> captain, and also the great triumphs he believes accompanied his role as Picard.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_film_and_television">Other film and television</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Patrick_Stewart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Other film and television">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Stewart's other film and television roles include the flamboyantly gay Sterling in the 1995 film <i><a href="/wiki/Jeffrey_(1995_film)" title="Jeffrey (1995 film)">Jeffrey</a></i> and <a href="/wiki/Henry_II_of_England" title="Henry II of England">King Henry II</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lion_in_Winter_(2003_film)" title="The Lion in Winter (2003 film)">The Lion in Winter</a></i>, for which he received a <a href="/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Golden Globe Award">Golden Globe Award</a> nomination for his performance and an <a href="/wiki/Emmy_Award" title="Emmy Award">Emmy Award</a> nomination for executive-producing the film. He portrayed <a href="/wiki/Ahab_(Moby-Dick)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ahab (Moby-Dick)">Captain Ahab</a> in the 1998 made-for-television film version of <i><a href="/wiki/Moby_Dick_(1998_miniseries)" title="Moby Dick (1998 miniseries)">Moby Dick</a></i>, receiving an Emmy Award nomination<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> and Golden Globe Award nomination for his performance. He also starred as <a href="/wiki/Ebenezer_Scrooge" title="Ebenezer Scrooge">Scrooge</a> in a 1999 <a href="/wiki/A_Christmas_Carol_(1999_film)" title="A Christmas Carol (1999 film)">television film version of Charles Dickens' <i>A Christmas Carol</i></a>, receiving a Screen Actors Guild Award nomination for his performance.
</p><p>In late 2003, during the 11th and final season of <a href="/wiki/NBC" title="NBC">NBC</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Frasier" title="Frasier">Frasier</a></i>, Stewart appeared on the show as a gay <a href="/wiki/Seattle" title="Seattle">Seattle</a> socialite and opera director, who mistakes <a href="/wiki/Frasier_Crane" title="Frasier Crane">Frasier</a> for a potential lover. In July 2003, he appeared in Series 2 (Episode 09) of <i><a href="/wiki/Top_Gear_(2002_TV_series)" title="Top Gear (2002 TV series)">Top Gear</a></i> in the <a href="/wiki/Star_in_a_Reasonably-Priced_Car" class="mw-redirect" title="Star in a Reasonably-Priced Car">Star in a Reasonably-Priced Car</a> segment, achieving a time of 1:50 in the <a href="/wiki/Suzuki_Liana" class="mw-redirect" title="Suzuki Liana">Liana</a>. In 2005, he was cast as Professor Ian Hood in an <a href="/wiki/ITV_(TV_network)" title="ITV (TV network)">ITV</a> thriller 4-episode series <i><a href="/wiki/Eleventh_Hour_(UK_TV_series)" class="mw-redirect" title="Eleventh Hour (UK TV series)">Eleventh Hour</a></i>, created by <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Gallagher" title="Stephen Gallagher">Stephen Gallagher</a>. The first episode was broadcast on 19 January 2006. He also, in 2005, played <a href="/wiki/Captain_Nemo" title="Captain Nemo">Captain Nemo</a> in a two-part adaptation of <i><a href="/wiki/Mysterious_Island_(2005_film)" title="Mysterious Island (2005 film)">The Mysterious Island</a></i>. Stewart also appeared as a nudity-obsessed caricature of himself in <a href="/wiki/Ricky_Gervais" title="Ricky Gervais">Ricky Gervais</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Merchant" title="Stephen Merchant">Stephen Merchant</a>'s television series <i><a href="/wiki/Extras_(TV_series)" title="Extras (TV series)">Extras</a></i>. In late 2018, it was announced that Stewart will play <a href="/wiki/John_Bosley_(Charlie%27s_Angels)" title="John Bosley (Charlie&#39;s Angels)">John Bosley</a> in the 2019 film <i><a href="/wiki/Charlie%27s_Angels_(2019_film)" title="Charlie&#39;s Angels (2019 film)">Charlie's Angels</a></i>, slated for release on 27 September 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Stage_.281990.E2.80.93present.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Stage_(1990–present)">Stage (1990–present)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Patrick_Stewart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Stage (1990–present)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>After <i>The Next Generation</i> began, Stewart soon found that he missed acting on the stage.<sup id="cite_ref-appleyard20071104_31-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-appleyard20071104-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> Although he remained associated with the Royal Shakespeare Company, the lengthy filming for the series had prevented him from participating in most other works, leaving a "gaping hole" of many years in his <a href="/wiki/Curriculum_vitae" title="Curriculum vitae">CV</a> as a Shakespearean actor, causing him to miss opportunities to play such notable roles as <a href="/wiki/Prince_Hamlet" title="Prince Hamlet">Hamlet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Romeo_Montague" class="mw-redirect" title="Romeo Montague">Romeo</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Richard_III_(play)" title="Richard III (play)">Richard III</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-appleyard20071104_31-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-appleyard20071104-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-lyall20080127_30-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lyall20080127-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Instead, Stewart began writing <a href="/wiki/One-man_show" class="mw-redirect" title="One-man show">one-man shows</a> that he performed in <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a> universities and acting schools. One of these—a version of <a href="/wiki/Charles_Dickens" title="Charles Dickens">Charles Dickens</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/A_Christmas_Carol" title="A Christmas Carol">A Christmas Carol</a></i> in which he portrayed all 40-plus characters—became ideal for him as an actor as well, because of its limited performing schedule.<sup id="cite_ref-collins19911215_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-collins19911215-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1991, Stewart performed it on Broadway,<sup id="cite_ref-appleyard20071104_31-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-appleyard20071104-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> receiving a nomination for that year's <a href="/wiki/Drama_Desk_Award_for_Outstanding_One-Person_Show" class="mw-redirect" title="Drama Desk Award for Outstanding One-Person Show">Drama Desk Award for Outstanding One-Person Show</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> He staged encore Broadway performances in 1992 and 1994, with the 1993 run held in London and the 1996 production in Los Angeles. Stewart brought the show back to Broadway in 2001, with all proceeds going to charity – and the show of 28 December's revenue, specifically, going to the <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">11 September</a> campaign of the <a href="/wiki/Actors_Fund_of_America" title="Actors Fund of America">Actors Fund of America</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> A 23-day run re-opened in London's West End in December 2005. For his performances in this play, Stewart has received the <a href="/wiki/Drama_Desk_Award" title="Drama Desk Award">Drama Desk Award</a> for Best Solo Performance in 1992 and the <a href="/wiki/Laurence_Olivier_Award" title="Laurence Olivier Award">Laurence Olivier Award</a> for Best Entertainment for Solo Performance in 1994. He was also the <a href="/wiki/Theatrical_producer" title="Theatrical producer">co-producer</a> of the show, through the company he set up for the purpose: Camm Lane Productions, a reference to his birthplace in Camm Lane, Mirfield.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:9.24.13WaitingForGodot-NoMansLandPressJunketByLuigiNovi8.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/9.24.13WaitingForGodot-NoMansLandPressJunketByLuigiNovi8.jpg/220px-9.24.13WaitingForGodot-NoMansLandPressJunketByLuigiNovi8.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/9.24.13WaitingForGodot-NoMansLandPressJunketByLuigiNovi8.jpg/330px-9.24.13WaitingForGodot-NoMansLandPressJunketByLuigiNovi8.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/9.24.13WaitingForGodot-NoMansLandPressJunketByLuigiNovi8.jpg/440px-9.24.13WaitingForGodot-NoMansLandPressJunketByLuigiNovi8.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2102" data-file-height="2106" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:9.24.13WaitingForGodot-NoMansLandPressJunketByLuigiNovi8.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Stewart with actors <a href="/wiki/Ian_McKellen" title="Ian McKellen">Ian McKellen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Billy_Crudup" title="Billy Crudup">Billy Crudup</a> at a 24 September 2013 press event at <a href="/wiki/Sardi%27s" title="Sardi&#39;s">Sardi's</a> restaurant for <i><a href="/wiki/Waiting_for_Godot" title="Waiting for Godot">Waiting for Godot</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/No_Man%27s_Land_(play)" title="No Man&#39;s Land (play)">No Man's Land</a></i></div></div></div>
<p>Shakespeare roles during this period included <a href="/wiki/Prospero" title="Prospero">Prospero</a> in Shakespeare's <i><a href="/wiki/The_Tempest_(play)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Tempest (play)">The Tempest</a></i>, on Broadway in 1995, a role he would reprise in <a href="/wiki/Rupert_Goold" title="Rupert Goold">Rupert Goold</a>'s 2006 production of <i>The Tempest</i> as part of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Shakespeare_Company" title="Royal Shakespeare Company">Royal Shakespeare Company</a>'s Complete Works Festival.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> In 1997, he took the role of Othello with the <a href="/wiki/Shakespeare_Theatre_Company" title="Shakespeare Theatre Company">Shakespeare Theatre Company</a> (<a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington, D.C.</a>) in a race-bending performance, in a "photo negative" production of a white <i>Othello</i> with an otherwise all-black cast. Stewart had wanted to play the title role since the age of 14, so he and director <a href="/wiki/Jude_Kelly" title="Jude Kelly">Jude Kelly</a> inverted the play so Othello became a comment on a white man entering a black society.<sup id="cite_ref-BMC1_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BMC1-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Othelloby_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Othelloby-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="quotebox pullquote floatleft" style="width:300px;&#32;;"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r887775652"/>
<div class="quotebox-quote left-aligned" style="">[London theatre] critics ... have showered him with perhaps the highest compliment they can conjure. He has, they say, overcome the technique-destroying indignity of being a major American television star.</div>
<p><cite class="right-aligned" style=""><i>The New York Times</i>, 2008<sup id="cite_ref-lyall20080127_30-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lyall20080127-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup></cite>
</p>
</div>
<p>He played Antony again opposite <a href="/wiki/Harriet_Walter" title="Harriet Walter">Harriet Walter</a>'s Cleopatra in <i><a href="/wiki/Antony_and_Cleopatra" title="Antony and Cleopatra">Antony and Cleopatra</a></i> at the <a href="/wiki/Novello_Theatre" title="Novello Theatre">Novello Theatre</a> in London in 2007 to excellent reviews.<sup id="cite_ref-lyall20080127_30-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lyall20080127-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> During this period, Stewart also addressed the <a href="/wiki/Durham_Union_Society" class="mw-redirect" title="Durham Union Society">Durham Union Society</a> on his life in film and theatre. When Stewart began playing <a href="/wiki/Macbeth_(Macbeth)" class="mw-redirect" title="Macbeth (Macbeth)">Macbeth</a> in the West End in 2007, some said that he was too old for the role; he and the show again received excellent reviews, with one critic calling Stewart "one of our finest Shakespearean actors".<sup id="cite_ref-appleyard20071104_31-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-appleyard20071104-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-lyall20080127_30-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lyall20080127-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> He was named as the next <a href="/wiki/Cameron_Mackintosh" title="Cameron Mackintosh">Cameron Mackintosh</a> Visiting Professor of Contemporary Theatre based at <a href="/wiki/St_Catherine%27s_College,_Oxford" title="St Catherine&#39;s College, Oxford">St Catherine's College</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Oxford" title="University of Oxford">Oxford</a> in January 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> In 2008, Stewart played <a href="/wiki/King_Claudius" title="King Claudius">King Claudius</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/Hamlet" title="Hamlet">Hamlet</a></i> alongside <a href="/wiki/David_Tennant" title="David Tennant">David Tennant</a>. He won the <a href="/wiki/Laurence_Olivier_Award" title="Laurence Olivier Award">Laurence Olivier Award</a> for Best Supporting Actor for the part. When collecting his award, he dedicated the award "in part" to Tennant and Tennant's understudy Edward Bennett, after Tennant's back injury and subsequent absence from four weeks of <i>Hamlet</i> disqualified him from an Olivier nomination.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2009, Stewart appeared alongside <a href="/wiki/Ian_McKellen" title="Ian McKellen">Ian McKellen</a> as the lead duo of Vladimir (Didi) and Estragon (Gogo), in <i><a href="/wiki/Waiting_for_Godot" title="Waiting for Godot">Waiting for Godot</a></i>. Stewart had previously appeared only once alongside McKellen on stage, but the pair had developed a close friendship while waiting around on set filming the <i>X-Men</i> films.<sup id="cite_ref-Cav_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cav-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> Stewart stated that performing in this play was the fulfilment of a 50-year ambition, having seen <a href="/wiki/Peter_O%27Toole" title="Peter O&#39;Toole">Peter O'Toole</a> appear in it at the <a href="/wiki/Bristol_Old_Vic" title="Bristol Old Vic">Bristol Old Vic</a> while Stewart was just 17.<sup id="cite_ref-Cav_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cav-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> Reviewers stated that his interpretation captured well the balance between humour and despair that characterises the work.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Voice_acting">Voice acting</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Patrick_Stewart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Voice acting">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Patrick_Stewart_2012.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Patrick_Stewart_2012.jpg/170px-Patrick_Stewart_2012.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="213" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Patrick_Stewart_2012.jpg/255px-Patrick_Stewart_2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Patrick_Stewart_2012.jpg/340px-Patrick_Stewart_2012.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2291" data-file-height="2864" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Patrick_Stewart_2012.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Stewart at the <a href="/wiki/Peabody_Award" title="Peabody Award">71st Annual Peabody Awards Luncheon</a> 2012</div></div></div>
<p>Known for his strong and authoritative voice, Stewart has lent his voice to a number of projects. He has narrated recordings of <a href="/wiki/Sergei_Prokofiev" title="Sergei Prokofiev">Prokofiev</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Peter_and_the_Wolf" title="Peter and the Wolf">Peter and the Wolf</a></i> (winning a <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Spoken_Word_Album_for_Children" title="Grammy Award for Best Spoken Word Album for Children">Grammy</a>), <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Vivaldi" title="Antonio Vivaldi">Vivaldi</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_Four_Seasons_(Vivaldi)" title="The Four Seasons (Vivaldi)">The Four Seasons</a></i> (which had also been narrated by <a href="/wiki/William_Shatner" title="William Shatner">William Shatner</a><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>), <a href="/wiki/C._S._Lewis" title="C. S. Lewis">C. S. Lewis</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_Last_Battle" title="The Last Battle">The Last Battle</a></i> (conclusion of the series <i><a href="/wiki/The_Chronicles_of_Narnia" title="The Chronicles of Narnia">The Chronicles of Narnia</a></i>), <a href="/wiki/Rick_Wakeman" title="Rick Wakeman">Rick Wakeman</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Return_to_the_Centre_of_the_Earth" title="Return to the Centre of the Earth">Return to the Centre of the Earth</a></i>; as well as numerous TV programmes such as <i><a href="/wiki/High_Spirits_with_Shirley_Ghostman" title="High Spirits with Shirley Ghostman">High Spirits with Shirley Ghostman</a></i>. Stewart provided the narration for <i><a href="/wiki/Nine_Worlds" class="mw-redirect" title="Nine Worlds">Nine Worlds</a></i>, an astronomical tour of the <a href="/wiki/Solar_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Solar system">solar system</a> and nature documentaries such as <i>The Secret of Life on Earth</i> and <i>Mountain Gorilla</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> He is also heard as the voice of the Magic Mirror in <a href="/wiki/Disneyland_Park_(Anaheim)" class="mw-redirect" title="Disneyland Park (Anaheim)">Disneyland</a>'s live show, <i>Snow White – An Enchanting Musical</i>. He also was the narrator for the American release of <i><a href="/wiki/Dragons:_A_Fantasy_Made_Real" class="mw-redirect" title="Dragons: A Fantasy Made Real">Dragons: A Fantasy Made Real</a></i>. He is narrator for two fulldome video shows produced and distributed by Loch Ness Productions, called <i>MarsQuest</i> and <i>The Voyager Encounters</i>.
</p><p>He also was a voice actor on the animated films <i><a href="/wiki/The_Prince_of_Egypt" title="The Prince of Egypt">The Prince of Egypt</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Neutron:_Boy_Genius_(film)" class="mw-redirect" title="Jimmy Neutron: Boy Genius (film)">Jimmy Neutron: Boy Genius</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Chicken_Little_(2005_film)" title="Chicken Little (2005 film)">Chicken Little</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Pagemaster" title="The Pagemaster">The Pagemaster</a></i>, the English <a href="/wiki/Dubbing_(filmmaking)" title="Dubbing (filmmaking)">dubbings</a> of the Japanese <a href="/wiki/Anime" title="Anime">anime</a> films <i><a href="/wiki/Nausica%C3%A4_of_the_Valley_of_the_Wind_(film)" title="Nausicaä of the Valley of the Wind (film)">Nausicaä of the Valley of the Wind</a></i>, by <a href="/wiki/Hayao_Miyazaki" title="Hayao Miyazaki">Hayao Miyazaki</a>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Steamboy" title="Steamboy">Steamboy</a></i>, by <a href="/wiki/Katsuhiro_Otomo" title="Katsuhiro Otomo">Katsuhiro Otomo</a>, and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Emoji_Movie" title="The Emoji Movie">The Emoji Movie</a></i>. He supported his home town of <a href="/wiki/Dewsbury" title="Dewsbury">Dewsbury</a> in <a href="/wiki/West_Yorkshire" title="West Yorkshire">West Yorkshire</a> by lending his voice to a series of videos on the town in 1999. He voiced the pig <a href="/wiki/Napoleon_(Animal_Farm)" title="Napoleon (Animal Farm)">Napoleon</a> in a <a href="/wiki/Animal_Farm_(1999_film)" title="Animal Farm (1999 film)">made-for-TV film adaptation</a> of <a href="/wiki/George_Orwell" title="George Orwell">George Orwell</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Animal_Farm" title="Animal Farm">Animal Farm</a></i> and guest starred in the <i><a href="/wiki/The_Simpsons" title="The Simpsons">Simpsons</a></i> episode "<a href="/wiki/Homer_the_Great" title="Homer the Great">Homer the Great</a>" as Number One. Stewart also recorded a narration planned for the prologue and epilogue for Tim Burton's <i><a href="/wiki/The_Nightmare_Before_Christmas" title="The Nightmare Before Christmas">The Nightmare Before Christmas</a></i> but the final movie use another voice (the original narration appears only on the first edition of the film's soundtrack).
</p><p>He plays a recurring role as <a href="/wiki/CIA" class="mw-redirect" title="CIA">CIA</a> Deputy Director <a href="/wiki/Avery_Bullock" class="mw-redirect" title="Avery Bullock">Avery Bullock</a>, lending his likeness as well as his voice on the animated series <i><a href="/wiki/American_Dad!" title="American Dad!">American Dad!</a></i>. He has made (as of 6 August 2011) nine guest appearances on <i><a href="/wiki/Family_Guy" title="Family Guy">Family Guy</a></i> in various roles: first in "<a href="/wiki/Peter%27s_Got_Woods" title="Peter&#39;s Got Woods">Peter's Got Woods</a>", second in "<a href="/wiki/No_Meals_on_Wheels" title="No Meals on Wheels">No Meals on Wheels</a>" when Peter likens something to when he once swapped voices with him for a day, third in "<a href="/wiki/Lois_Kills_Stewie" class="mw-redirect" title="Lois Kills Stewie">Lois Kills Stewie</a>" as his <i>American Dad!</i> character Bullock, fourth in "<a href="/wiki/Not_All_Dogs_Go_to_Heaven" title="Not All Dogs Go to Heaven">Not All Dogs Go to Heaven</a>" as himself, fifth in  "<a href="/wiki/And_Then_There_Were_Fewer" title="And Then There Were Fewer">And Then There Were Fewer</a>" as a cat that proclaims himself a professor, sixth in "<a href="/wiki/Halloween_on_Spooner_Street" title="Halloween on Spooner Street">Halloween on Spooner Street</a>" as Dick Pump, seventh in "<a href="/wiki/The_Hand_That_Rocks_the_Wheelchair" title="The Hand That Rocks the Wheelchair">The Hand That Rocks the Wheelchair</a>" as Susie Swanson and eighth in the DVD version of <i><a href="/wiki/It%27s_A_Trap!" class="mw-redirect" title="It&#39;s A Trap!">It's A Trap!</a></i> as Picard. He also appears as a guest character in the mobile game Family Guy: The Quest For Stuff's Comicon event. To unlock him, you need to give him 1,000 Blam! drinks, 10 wizard books and 15 pizza slices before 8 September 2014.  Stewart also appears as narrator in <a href="/wiki/Seth_MacFarlane" title="Seth MacFarlane">Seth MacFarlane</a>'s 2012 film directorial debut, <i>Ted</i>. In 2006, Stewart voiced Bambi's father, the Great Prince of the Forest in Disney's direct-to-video sequel, <i><a href="/wiki/Bambi_II" title="Bambi II">Bambi II</a></i>.
</p><p>He lent his voice to the <a href="/wiki/Activision" title="Activision">Activision</a>-produced <i>Star Trek</i> computer games <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Trek:_Armada" title="Star Trek: Armada">Star Trek: Armada</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Trek:_Armada_II" title="Star Trek: Armada II">Armada II</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Trek:_Starfleet_Command_III" title="Star Trek: Starfleet Command III">Star Trek: Starfleet Command III</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Trek:_Invasion" title="Star Trek: Invasion">Star Trek: Invasion</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Trek:_Bridge_Commander" title="Star Trek: Bridge Commander">Bridge Commander</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Trek:_Elite_Force_II" title="Star Trek: Elite Force II">Elite Force II</a></i>, all reprising his role as Picard. Stewart reprised his role as Picard in <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Trek:_Legacy" title="Star Trek: Legacy">Star Trek: Legacy</a></i> for both PC and Xbox 360, along with the four other "major" Starfleet captains from the different Star Trek series.
</p><p>In addition to voicing his characters from <i>Star Trek</i> and <i>X-Men</i> in several related <a href="/wiki/Video_game" title="Video game">computer and video games</a>, Stewart worked as a voice actor on games unrelated to both franchises, such as <i><a href="/wiki/Castlevania:_Lords_of_Shadow" title="Castlevania: Lords of Shadow">Castlevania: Lords of Shadow</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Forgotten_Realms:_Demon_Stone" title="Forgotten Realms: Demon Stone">Forgotten Realms: Demon Stone</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Lands_of_Lore:_The_Throne_of_Chaos" title="Lands of Lore: The Throne of Chaos">Lands of Lore: The Throne of Chaos</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Elder_Scrolls_IV:_Oblivion" title="The Elder Scrolls IV: Oblivion">The Elder Scrolls IV: Oblivion</a></i> for which in 2006 he won a <a href="/wiki/Spike_TV_Video_Game_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="Spike TV Video Game Awards">Spike TV Video Game Award</a><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> for his work as Emperor Uriel Septim. He also lent his voice to several editions of the <i><a href="/wiki/Compton%27s_Encyclopedia" title="Compton&#39;s Encyclopedia">Compton's Interactive Encyclopedia</a></i>.
</p><p>His voice talents also appeared in a number of commercials including the UK TV adverts for the relaunch of <a href="/wiki/TSB_Bank_(United_Kingdom)" title="TSB Bank (United Kingdom)">TSB Bank</a>, Domestos bleach and <a href="/wiki/Moneysupermarket.com" title="Moneysupermarket.com">Moneysupermarket.com</a>, an advertisement for Shell fuel and an American advertisement for the prescription drug <a href="/wiki/Crestor" class="mw-redirect" title="Crestor">Crestor</a>. He also voiced the UK and Australian TV advertisements for the PAL version of <i><a href="/wiki/Final_Fantasy_XII" title="Final Fantasy XII">Final Fantasy XII</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Stewart used his voice for <a href="/wiki/Pontiac" title="Pontiac">Pontiac</a> and <a href="/wiki/Porsche" title="Porsche">Porsche</a> cars and <a href="/wiki/MasterCard" class="mw-redirect" title="MasterCard">MasterCard</a> Gold commercials in 1996, and <a href="/wiki/Goodyear_Tire_and_Rubber_Company" title="Goodyear Tire and Rubber Company">Goodyear</a> Assurance Tyres in 2004. He also did voice-overs for RCA televisions. He provided the voice of Max Winters in <i><a href="/wiki/TMNT_(film)" title="TMNT (film)">TMNT</a></i> in March 2007. In 2008, he was also the voice of television advertisements for <a href="/wiki/Currys" title="Currys">Currys</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stella_Artois" title="Stella Artois">Stella Artois</a> beer. Currently, he is heard during <a href="/wiki/National_Car_Rental" title="National Car Rental">National Car Rental</a> television spots.
</p><p>He voiced the narrator of the <a href="/wiki/Electronic_Arts" title="Electronic Arts">Electronic Arts</a> computer game, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Sims_Medieval" title="The Sims Medieval">The Sims Medieval</a></i>, for the game's introduction cinematic and trailer released on 22 March 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> He also voiced the story plaques and trailer of the <a href="/wiki/MMOG" class="mw-redirect" title="MMOG">MMOG</a> <i><a href="/wiki/LEGO_Universe" class="mw-redirect" title="LEGO Universe">LEGO Universe</a></i>.  In 2016, he narrated "The Connected Universe", a crowdfunded film directed by Malcolm Carter on the ideas of self-styled physicist Nassim Haramein.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Charity_work_and_activism">Charity work and activism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Patrick_Stewart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Charity work and activism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2006, Stewart made a short video against <a href="/wiki/Domestic_violence" title="Domestic violence">domestic violence</a> for <a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">Amnesty International</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> in which he recollected his father's physical attacks on his mother and the effect it had on him as a child. For instance, he said, "the physical harm ... [was] a shocking pain. But there are other aspects of violence which have more lasting impact psychologically on family members. It is destructive and tainting. As a child witnessing these events, one cannot simply help somehow feeling responsible for them; for the pain, and the screaming, and the misery."<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> In the same year, he gave his name to a scholarship at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Huddersfield" title="University of Huddersfield">University of Huddersfield</a>, where he is Chancellor, to fund post-graduate study into domestic violence.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> Stewart's childhood experience also led him to become a patron of <a href="/wiki/Refuge_(United_Kingdom_charity)" title="Refuge (United Kingdom charity)">Refuge</a>, a UK charity for abused women.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2009, Stewart gave a speech at the launch of <i>Created Equal,</i> a book about women's rights, talking again about his personal experiences with domestic violence and the impacts they had on him.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> He remarked, "violence is a choice and it's a choice a man makes ... the lasting impact on my mother...and indeed on myself ... was extreme. Overcoming the lessons of that male stereotype that I was being shown was a struggle."<sup id="cite_ref-:0_70-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> He now hopes to set an example of "what it has been like to be in an environment of such violence and that it can pass and that one can survive it and even though sometimes still a struggle."<sup id="cite_ref-:0_70-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> Additionally, in October 2011, he presented a BBC Lifeline Appeal on behalf of Refuge, discussing his own experience of domestic violence and interviewing a woman whose daughter was murdered by her ex-husband.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Stewart has supported the armed forces charity <a href="/wiki/Combat_Stress" class="mw-redirect" title="Combat Stress">Combat Stress</a>, since learning about his father's <a href="/wiki/Post-traumatic_stress" class="mw-redirect" title="Post-traumatic stress">post-traumatic stress</a> disorder when researching his family genealogy for the documentary series <i><a href="/wiki/Who_Do_You_Think_You_Are%3F_(UK_TV_series)" class="mw-redirect" title="Who Do You Think You Are? (UK TV series)">Who Do You Think You Are?</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> He is patron of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Association_UK" class="mw-redirect" title="United Nations Association UK">United Nations Association – UK</a>, and delivered a speech at UNA-UK's UN Forum 2012 on Saturday 14 July 2012,<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> speaking of his father's experiences in the <a href="/wiki/Second_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second World War">Second World War</a>, and how he believed that the UN was the best legacy of that period.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 15 April 2018 Stewart attended the launch event of the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Vote" title="People&#39;s Vote">People's Vote</a>, a campaign group calling for a public vote on the final <a href="/wiki/Brexit" title="Brexit">Brexit</a> deal between the UK and the European Union.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Patrick_Stewart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Relationships_and_children">Relationships and children</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Patrick_Stewart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Relationships and children">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Patrick_Stewart_Met_Opera_2010_Shankbone.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Patrick_Stewart_Met_Opera_2010_Shankbone.jpg/170px-Patrick_Stewart_Met_Opera_2010_Shankbone.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="226" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Patrick_Stewart_Met_Opera_2010_Shankbone.jpg/255px-Patrick_Stewart_Met_Opera_2010_Shankbone.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Patrick_Stewart_Met_Opera_2010_Shankbone.jpg/340px-Patrick_Stewart_Met_Opera_2010_Shankbone.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1623" data-file-height="2153" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Patrick_Stewart_Met_Opera_2010_Shankbone.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Stewart at the 2010 <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Opera" title="Metropolitan Opera">Metropolitan Opera</a>'s opening night of <i><a href="/wiki/Das_Rheingold" title="Das Rheingold">Das Rheingold</a></i></div></div></div>
<p>Stewart and his first wife, Sheila Falconer, <a href="/wiki/Divorce" title="Divorce">divorced</a> in 1990 after 24 years of marriage.<sup id="cite_ref-Ritter_Remembered_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ritter_Remembered-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-independent2009_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-independent2009-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> They have two children, son Daniel and daughter Sophia.<sup id="cite_ref-independent2009_77-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-independent2009-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> Daniel is a television actor,<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> and has appeared alongside his father in the 1993 <a href="/wiki/Made-for-television" class="mw-redirect" title="Made-for-television">made-for-television</a> film <i><a href="/wiki/Death_Train" title="Death Train">Death Train</a></i>, and in the 1992 <i>Star Trek: The Next Generation</i> episode "<a href="/wiki/The_Inner_Light_(Star_Trek:_The_Next_Generation)" title="The Inner Light (Star Trek: The Next Generation)">The Inner Light</a>", playing his son.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;n 1&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1997, Stewart became engaged to Wendy Neuss, one of the producers of <i>Star Trek: The Next Generation</i>. They married on 25 August 2000, and divorced three years later.<sup id="cite_ref-Ritter_Remembered_76-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ritter_Remembered-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;n 2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-independent2009_77-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-independent2009-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Four months before his divorce from Neuss, Stewart played opposite actress <a href="/wiki/Lisa_Dillon" title="Lisa Dillon">Lisa Dillon</a> in a production of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Master_Builder" title="The Master Builder">The Master Builder</a></i>, and the two were romantically involved until 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2008, Stewart began dating <a href="/wiki/Sunny_Ozell" title="Sunny Ozell">Sunny Ozell</a>, a singer and songwriter based in <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn" title="Brooklyn">Brooklyn</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York</a>, whom Stewart met while performing in <i><a href="/wiki/Macbeth_(play)" class="mw-redirect" title="Macbeth (play)">Macbeth</a></i> at the <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Academy_of_Music" title="Brooklyn Academy of Music">Brooklyn Academy of Music</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-nytimes2013_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes2013-83">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> Stewart purchased a home in <a href="/wiki/Park_Slope" title="Park Slope">Park Slope</a>, in August 2012,<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> and subsequently began living there with Ozell.<sup id="cite_ref-nytimes2013_83-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes2013-83">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> In March 2013, it was reported that Stewart and Ozell were engaged,<sup id="cite_ref-nytimes2013_83-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes2013-83">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> and they married in September 2013 with Sir <a href="/wiki/Ian_McKellen" title="Ian McKellen">Ian McKellen</a> performing the wedding ceremony.<sup id="cite_ref-nytimes2013_83-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes2013-83">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Beliefs.2C_causes_and_interests"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Beliefs,_causes_and_interests">Beliefs, causes and interests</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Patrick_Stewart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Beliefs, causes and interests">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Stewart has stated that his politics are rooted in a belief in fairness and <a href="/wiki/Social_equality" title="Social equality">equality</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-back_on_stage_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-back_on_stage-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> He considers himself a <a href="/wiki/Socialism" title="Socialism">socialist</a> and was a member of the <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour Party</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ind20030630_21-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ind20030630-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-xfactor_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-xfactor-86">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> He stated, "My father was a very strong <a href="/wiki/Trade_union" title="Trade union">trade unionist</a> and those fundamental issues of Labour were ingrained into me."<sup id="cite_ref-xfactor_86-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-xfactor-86">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> He was critical of the <a href="/wiki/Iraq_War" title="Iraq War">Iraq War</a> and UK government legislation in the area of <a href="/wiki/Civil_liberties" title="Civil liberties">civil liberties</a>, in particular its plans to extend <a href="/wiki/Counter-Terrorism_Act_2008#42_day_terrorist_detention_without_charge" title="Counter-Terrorism Act 2008">detention without charge to 42 days for terrorist suspects</a>. He signed an open letter of objection to this proposal in March 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> In August 2018 Stewart announced he had left Labour due to concerns over the leadership of <a href="/wiki/Jeremy_Corbyn" title="Jeremy Corbyn">Jeremy Corbyn</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> Stewart is a patron of <a href="/wiki/Humanists_UK" title="Humanists UK">Humanists UK</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> He also identifies himself as a feminist.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> He has publicly advocated the right to <a href="/wiki/Assisted_suicide" title="Assisted suicide">assisted suicide</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-chri_Patr_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chri_Patr-93">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> In January 2011, Stewart became a patron for <a href="/wiki/Dignity_in_Dying" title="Dignity in Dying">Dignity in Dying</a> and campaigns for an assisted dying law in the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In August 2014, Stewart was one of 200 public figures who were signatories to a letter to <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> expressing their hope that <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a> would vote to remain part of the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> in September's <a href="/wiki/2014_Scottish_independence_referendum" title="2014 Scottish independence referendum">referendum on that issue</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2016, Stewart, along with <a href="/wiki/Benedict_Cumberbatch" title="Benedict Cumberbatch">Benedict Cumberbatch</a>, led more than 280 figures from the arts world who backed a vote to remain in the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">EU</a> in regards to the <a href="/wiki/2016_United_Kingdom_European_Union_membership_referendum" title="2016 United Kingdom European Union membership referendum">referendum</a> on that issue.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 2 March 2017, Stewart said he was going to apply for <a href="/wiki/Citizenship_of_the_United_States" title="Citizenship of the United States">US citizenship</a> in order to oppose the <a href="/wiki/Presidency_of_Donald_Trump" title="Presidency of Donald Trump">Trump administration</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> However, in an interview by the <a href="/wiki/Press_Association" class="mw-redirect" title="Press Association">Press Association</a> at the <a href="/wiki/British_Film_Institute" title="British Film Institute">British Film Institute</a> Luminous Fundraising Gala on 3 October 2017, Stewart said that he hoped the US would pass <a href="/wiki/Gun_laws_in_the_United_States_by_state" title="Gun laws in the United States by state">stronger gun laws</a>, but did not mention any intention of becoming an American citizen in furtherance of that hope.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Stewart is a lifelong supporter of his local <a href="/wiki/Association_Football" class="mw-redirect" title="Association Football">football</a> club <a href="/wiki/Huddersfield_Town_A.F.C." title="Huddersfield Town A.F.C.">Huddersfield Town A.F.C.</a><sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> He was at Wembley Stadium in 2017 when the club won promotion to the <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">top division</a> for the first time since 1972.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> Since 2010, he has been president of <a href="/wiki/Huddersfield_Town_F.C._Reserves_and_Academy" class="mw-redirect" title="Huddersfield Town F.C.
